  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4fcc4745-1ead-4073-ba44-bb434abff3f5'

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028283353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1119526603753631934">Tove Jansson is really kind of amazing. <br/><br/>This is only the second books of hers I've read, the other being <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79550.The_Summer_Book' title='The Summer Book by Tove Jansson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Summer Book</a>. I was impressed then by the subtlety of her writing and her nuanced depiction of complex, contradictory human beings, but I wasn't entirely surprised -- it was an adult book, written about people Jansson knew well personally. I was not expecting a short children's book about cute made up creatures to display the same level of insights into human nature and behavior. But it to</span>
  <span id="freeText1119526603753631934" style="display:none">Tove Jansson is really kind of amazing. <br /><br />This is only the second books of hers I've read, the other being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79550.The_Summer_Book" title="The Summer Book by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer Book</a>. I was impressed then by the subtlety of her writing and her nuanced depiction of complex, contradictory human beings, but I wasn't entirely surprised -- it was an adult book, written about people Jansson knew well personally. I was not expecting a short children's book about cute made up creatures to display the same level of insights into human nature and behavior. But it totally does. It's not heavy-handed; if you're a small child mostly interested in the fun adventures of Moomins you can totally read it just for that. You won't be slapped in the face by the fact that people are sometimes needless cruel, or unhappy for no good reason, misunderstand one another, hate themselves... But they do. They do. Even if they are cuddly trolls.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12250424831250930065"><b>The Moomin family wild adventures starting with a volcano and a flood which separates them - for a while</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581663712i/28961230._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='375' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Why do volcanoes annoy us so?</i><br/>Moominmamma rose with a sigh.<br/>‘So very annoying, this volcano,’ she remarked.<br/>‘Volcano?’ asked Little My, and thrust an interested head out of the wool.<br/>‘Yes, it’s a mountain not so very far from here, and all of a sudden it’s begun spitting fire and smoke over the whole valley,’ explained Moominmamma. ‘And soot. It’s always kept quiet and good ever since I married. A</span>
  <span id="freeText12250424831250930065" style="display:none"><b>The Moomin family wild adventures starting with a volcano and a flood which separates them - for a while</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581663712i/28961230._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Why do volcanoes annoy us so?</i><br>Moominmamma rose with a sigh.<br>‘So very annoying, this volcano,’ she remarked.<br>‘Volcano?’ asked Little My, and thrust an interested head out of the wool.<br>‘Yes, it’s a mountain not so very far from here, and all of a sudden it’s begun spitting fire and smoke over the whole valley,’ explained Moominmamma. ‘And soot. It’s always kept quiet and good ever since I married. And now, after all these years, exactly when I’ve finished my washing, it has to sneeze once again and blacken all the things I hang out.’<br>‘Everybody’s burning up!’ shouted Little My happily, ‘And everybody’s houses and gardens and playthings and little sisters and their playthings!’<br>‘Fiddlesticks,’ said Moominmamma genially and whisked away another speck of soot from her snout.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581663712i/28961231._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Is the flood going to take them all to heaven?</i><br>It was at that moment they heard the great rumble.<br>It came rolling up from across the sea, first low and mumbling, then growing stronger and stronger.<br>In the fair night they could see something enormous rise high over the tree-tops of the forest, like a great wall that grew and grew with a white and foaming crest.<br>‘I suppose we’d better go into the drawing-room now,’ said Moominmamma.<br>They had no more than got their tails inside the door when the flood wave came crashing through the Moomin Valley and drenched everything in darkness. The house rocked slightly but didn’t lose its foothold. It was soundly built and a very good house. But after a while the drawing-room furniture began to float around. The family then moved upstairs and sat down to wait for the storm to blow over.<br>‘I haven’t seen such weather since my young days,’ said Moominpappa brightly and lit a candle.<br>Outside the night was in full uproar, cracking and banging things about and thumping heavy waves against the shutters.<br>Moominmamma absentmindedly seated herself in the rocking-chair and set it slowly rocking.<br>‘Is this the end of the world?’ Little My asked curiously.<br>‘That’s the very least,’ replied the Mymble’s daughter. ‘Try to be good now if you can find the time, because in a little while we’re all going to heaven.’<br>‘Heaven?’ asked Little My. ‘Do we have to? And how does one get down again?’<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581663712i/28961232.jpg" width="400" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>At last everyone could understand the play</i><br>The spectators now saw the Mymble’s daughter lifting Little My in her arms and getting kissed on the nose, and they noticed that nobody spoke in blank verse any longer, but quite naturally. This met with general approval, because now it was finally possible to understand what the play was about.<br>It was about someone who had floated away from home, and had awful experiences, and now found her way home again. And everybody was marvellously happy and going to have a cup of tea.<br>‘They’re playing a lot better now, I think,’ said the Hemulen.<br>Snufkin began to hoist all his woodies up on to the stage. ‘Hello, Moominmamma!’ he cried happily. ‘Can you take care of these for me?’<br>The play became funnier and funnier. By and by, the whole of the audience came climbing up on the stage and took part in the plot by beginning to eat the entrance fees that were laid out on the drawing-room table. Moominmamma freed herself from the troublesome skirts and rushed to and fro serving out teacups.<br>The band started on the Hemulic Triumphal March.<br>Moominpappa was radiant with the great success, and Misabel was every bit as happy as at the dress rehearsal.<br>Suddenly Moominmamma stopped in the middle of the stage and dropped a teacup to the floor.<br>‘Here he comes,’ she whispered, and everybody became silent.<br>Out in the dark a faint sound of oars came nearer. A clear little bell was tinkling.<br>‘Mother!’ somebody was shouting. ‘Father! I’m coming home!’<br>‘Indeed,’ said the Hemulen. ‘My own prisoners! Catch them at once before they burn the theatre down!’<br>Moominmamma rushed up to the footlights. She saw Moomintroll lose hold of one of his oars when he was about to lay to. Confusedly he tried to pull with the remaining one, but his boat only spun round on the spot. In the stern sat a thin little Hemulen with a kind sort of face and shouting something nobody took any notice of.<br>‘Flee!’ cried Moominmamma. ‘The police are here!’<br>She didn’t know what her Moomintroll had done, but she was convinced that she approved of it.<br><br><b>Moominmamma has absolute faith in her extended family surviving any disasters and that they will always be together. <br>A Happily Ever After ending!</b><br><br><br>Enjoy!<br><br><br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56725585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16616836275728381805">I've liked all Moomin books this far, but somehow this one appealed to me even more than usual. The writing style and the atmosphere of the story are exactly as magical as they should be on a Midsummer night, and despite the rather absurd and adventurous happenings the book left me with a very peaceful mood. There's almost something Shakespearean in this, even though there are no fairies. The play within the story is hilarious, and the whole theatre thing just made me laugh so much. I also fangi</span>
  <span id="freeText16616836275728381805" style="display:none">I've liked all Moomin books this far, but somehow this one appealed to me even more than usual. The writing style and the atmosphere of the story are exactly as magical as they should be on a Midsummer night, and despite the rather absurd and adventurous happenings the book left me with a very peaceful mood. There's almost something Shakespearean in this, even though there are no fairies. The play within the story is hilarious, and the whole theatre thing just made me laugh so much. I also fangirl Snufkin and this book shows some sides of his personality very well.</span>

<div id="review_2654420237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2654420237" />
    <a title="Paula Bardell-Hedley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53441266-paula-bardell-hedley"><img alt="Paula Bardell-Hedley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500050221p2/53441266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2654420237?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula Bardell-Hedley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula Bardell-Hedley" href="/user/show/53441266-paula-bardell-hedley">Paula Bardell-Hedley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781908745699" href="/book/show/39781728-moominsummer-madness">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Moominites of every age!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53441266-paula-bardell-hedley?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53441266-paula-bardell-hedley?shelf=translated-literature">translated-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2654420237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15163778732067065064"><blockquote>
  <i>“A theatre is the most important sort of house in the world, because that’s where people are shown what they could be if they wanted, and what they’d like to be if they dared to and what they really are.”</i>
</blockquote><i>Moominsummer Madness</i> is the fourth title in Tove Jansson’s series of stories about a family of benevolent, philosophical trolls with downy fur and soft round snouts, who reside in a rather unusual house in an attractive woodland valley by the sea.<br/><br/>Moominites tend to consider this book, first </span>
  <span id="freeText15163778732067065064" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“A theatre is the most important sort of house in the world, because that’s where people are shown what they could be if they wanted, and what they’d like to be if they dared to and what they really are.”</i>
</blockquote><i>Moominsummer Madness</i> is the fourth title in Tove Jansson’s series of stories about a family of benevolent, philosophical trolls with downy fur and soft round snouts, who reside in a rather unusual house in an attractive woodland valley by the sea.<br /><br />Moominites tend to consider this book, first published in 1954, the final title in the series written with only children in mind. As with the earlier stories, the scenery is pleasingly verdant, but the setting isn’t specifically Finnish, and the plot is driven by a natural disaster as opposed to internal conflict. <br /><br />The story begins with a rumbling volcano, raining ash down on Moominmamma’s clean washing, leading to Moominvalley being flooded. The family are forced to leave their beloved home and seek sanctuary on a floating theatre. However, they are deliberately cast adrift during the night, leaving Moomintroll, the Snork Maiden and Little My stranded (on account of them sleeping in a tree). Much Moomin summer madness follows and we are left wondering if they will find each other before taking their final bows.<br /><br />We are at a point in the series when Jansson knew the characters well and they had become familiar to her readers – she therefore does not attempt any kind of introduction – indeed, there is little need to as her wonderfully idiosyncratic illustrations do the job perfectly. These individuals are often given onomatopoeic names, for example, Whomper, who appears for the first time in this book. He is a serious but kindly little fellow with large, dark eyes and a messy head of hair who wears a black coat and a scarf around his neck, held together with a safety pin. His name is <i>Homsan</i> in Swedish, meaning rush about or do something carelessly, often with unfortunate results. The name suits him well because although he tries hard to comprehend the world around him, he finds it utterly baffling. He does, however, discover his perfect vocation in the theatre.<br /><br />There is much irony and artful humour in all Jansson’s Moomin books, though never at the expense of her child readers, and <i>Moominsummer Madness</i> is no exception. The characters’ feelings and the difficulties they experience are always of the utmost importance. In fact, it is often the adults in the story who behave irrationally while the young ones are filled with intelligent curiosity and an eagerness to please.<br /><br />The book captures the mood of summer: the lethargy, the afternoons spent gazing into water, the buzzing of bees and the balmy light nights. In many ways it isn’t dissimilar to Shakespeare’s <i>A Midsummer Night’s Dream</i>, in so much as characters often misconstrue one another’s words and actions and stubbornly continue to be desirous of things they cannot have or achieve. A play is also enacted in which there is a lion. <br /><br />I found re-reading this tale of Moomin wisdom and shenanigans every bit as charming and bizarre as I did as a child. Jansson’s unpredictable creatures and her anarchic illustrations are still able to captivate and amuse me almost 50 years on. <br /><br />My copy of the book is a Collector’s Edition Moomin Hardback published in 2018 by <a href="http://www.sortof.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Sort of Books</a>, which has been “lovingly restored” to its former striking design. It was translated by Thomas Warburton (1918-2016). Jansson dedicated it to her old-flame and lifelong friend, Vivica Bandler. It originally remained in print for over sixty years, appearing in more than fifty languages.<blockquote>
  <i> “Moomin people thank each other not only for tea but after every meal they eat together. They like to feel polite.”</i>
</blockquote><b>You can read more of my reviews and other literary features at <a href="https://bookjotter.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Jotter</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15163778732067065064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435730652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6142701628206763226">A volcano unleashes a tsunami that floods Moominvalley, causing the family, no more than mildly perturbed by the experience, to take refuge in a floating theater. Jansson pokes fun at the theatrical, the overly loquacious, the control freaks, and others, in way accessible to children and enjoyable to adults.<br/><br/>Lots of friends here are into the Moomins, and, now that I've read one, I can see why - "Moominsummer Madness" was a hoot. It's far down in the series, but it wasn't difficult to understand t</span>
  <span id="freeText6142701628206763226" style="display:none">A volcano unleashes a tsunami that floods Moominvalley, causing the family, no more than mildly perturbed by the experience, to take refuge in a floating theater. Jansson pokes fun at the theatrical, the overly loquacious, the control freaks, and others, in way accessible to children and enjoyable to adults.<br /><br />Lots of friends here are into the Moomins, and, now that I've read one, I can see why - "Moominsummer Madness" was a hoot. It's far down in the series, but it wasn't difficult to understand the characters and their personalities. This is the only one of Jansson's works in our useless library system, and it is rather battered. I hope I haven't triggered the librarians to cull it before I have the chance to read it to the kids. (Maybe I have enough renewal time left?)<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2875934674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2875934674" />
    <a title="Juushika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/616321-juushika"><img alt="Juushika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541586729p2/616321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2875934674?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juushika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juushika" href="/user/show/616321-juushika">Juushika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312608910" href="/book/show/7325411-moominsummer-madness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-childrens">genre-childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=status-borrowed">status-borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/616321-juushika?shelf=seasonal-summer">seasonal-summer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2875934674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8363923661560854381">Flood sends the Moomin family from their home during the height of June. Unbeknownst to them, they end up living in a <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[floating theatre <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I'll admit I'm not enamored of the dramatic irony and pastiche that this introduces; I love these books more when they're cozy/domestic or atmospheric/magical--funny/campy is less my vibe. But there's still so much cozy and atmospheric to be had. Multithreaded, coincidence-laden plots are difficult to pull off in more serious w</span>
  <span id="freeText8363923661560854381" style="display:none">Flood sends the Moomin family from their home during the height of June. Unbeknownst to them, they end up living in a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[floating theatre <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I'll admit I'm not enamored of the dramatic irony and pastiche that this introduces; I love these books more when they're cozy/domestic or atmospheric/magical--funny/campy is less my vibe. But there's still so much cozy and atmospheric to be had. Multithreaded, coincidence-laden plots are difficult to pull off in more serious works, but when the underlying theme is that things will work out, that characters will be reunited, a coincidental structure is soothing. And the reassurance of a happy ending opens the way for a contrasting but unthreatening sense of loss and loneliness. There's room for characters like mopey, quotable Misabel, who I love even more than Thingummy and Bob. And by coincidence I read this in late June, building on the book's atmosphere, late summer nights shimmering with quiet magic. I think this gets in its own way a little--it could be a perfect book; it's not, but it's a pleasure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8363923661560854381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1252535045" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1252535045" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5719060-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492889428p2/5719060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1252535045?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/5719060-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312608910" href="/book/show/7325411-moominsummer-madness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5719060-drew?shelf=read_to_kids">read_to_kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1252535045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2196522900720191828">I love these stories. They're ostensibly for children, but there's so much deep wisdom in these books that an adult mind will relish them. As I have been doing.<br/><br/>The book kicks off with the eruption of a volcano which causes a tsunami which floods Moominvalley, swamping the Moomin house up to the second floor. The reaction by the Moomins and their friends is one of resigned whimsy. Why not cut a hole in the floor in order to look down into the kitchen from above and see what it looks like underwat</span>
  <span id="freeText2196522900720191828" style="display:none">I love these stories. They're ostensibly for children, but there's so much deep wisdom in these books that an adult mind will relish them. As I have been doing.<br /><br />The book kicks off with the eruption of a volcano which causes a tsunami which floods Moominvalley, swamping the Moomin house up to the second floor. The reaction by the Moomins and their friends is one of resigned whimsy. Why not cut a hole in the floor in order to look down into the kitchen from above and see what it looks like underwater? Because of course.<br /><br />When a theater floats by on the flood, all the characters take shelter in it, not really knowing what a theater is or what it's for. The explanation by the theater's lone inhabitant seems to sum up the theme of the book:<br /><br /><i>"A theatre is the most important sort of house in the world, because that's where people are shown what they could be if they wanted, and what they'd like to be if they dared to and what they really are."<br /><br />"A reformatory!" said Moominmamma, astonished.</i><br /><br />The first half of the book seems imbued with sadness -- the (temporary) loss of a home, displacement (physically and emotionally) from family, the bitterness of the elderly stage rat.<br /><br />The theater becomes a place of exploration (outwardly as it literally floats down the river, but inwardly as characters explore the rooms of the theater, and ultimately themselves).<br /><br />The story spins off in all directions, stranding a pair of characters along the way, picking up some new ones, and looking in on frequent wanderer Snufkin on his return trip to the valley, causing anarchic mischief along the way. (Snufkin's personal war with authoritarian park keepers is a highlight.)<br /><br />I started out the book feeling unsatisfied with the turns of the plot. Perhaps I was simply feeling the dissatisfaction and unease of the characters themselves stuck in an uncertain situation. But by the end of the book, all the elements are woven together as the theater-bound characters decide to put on a play that turns into a comic fiasco. Ultimately, the book is just as satisfying as the rest of this series has been. Highly recommended.<br /><br />On the downside: Sniff is not in this book, and there is no explanation for it. What happened to Sniff?! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2196522900720191828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7611953474482461460" style="display:none"><b>Re-read 21.6.2020</b><br />From 3 stars to 3.5 stars.<br /><br />This is the only Moomin book that I always expect to be more magical and, I don't know, more summery I guess. That's not to say that it's not. I just don't personally get that feeling or love it as much as I'd like to, even though it's set during Midsummer.<br /><br />Overall, it's a fun adventure during a flood. The magic of theater turns out to be more difficult to create than the Moomin family ever thought, Snufkin tries his hand as a foster father, and some of our friends end up in jail, but eventually it's time to return home. The magic of Midsummer feels like a dream when ordinary and familiar life resurfaces from under the water. It's only the beginning of summer and further adventures await!</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3614074-les?shelf=crazyasssprintbeforestudentteaching">crazyasssprintbeforestudentteaching</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465874110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2881148557248537224">Wonderful. Few things are more fun to read with my kids than the Moomins. Tove Jansson is one of a kind.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2774355015" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12353805-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518454186p2/12353805.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774355015?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/12353805-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140305012" href="/book/show/1244094.Moominsummer_Madness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12353805-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774355015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6252040566457153460">The Moomins get cuter as books go by, and there's also far more characters accompanying them. We've got the Mymble's daughter and Little My, more Hemulens, all the theatre people, plus Whoomper and Misabel. <br/>The story is about a flood in Moomin valley and how the family ends up living in a theatre for a while, which ends up being really fun as they even put up a play. Misabel was a horrible character at the beginning, she's always sad and lonely, but it gets better later on. I loved the small the</span>
  <span id="freeText6252040566457153460" style="display:none">The Moomins get cuter as books go by, and there's also far more characters accompanying them. We've got the Mymble's daughter and Little My, more Hemulens, all the theatre people, plus Whoomper and Misabel. <br />The story is about a flood in Moomin valley and how the family ends up living in a theatre for a while, which ends up being really fun as they even put up a play. Misabel was a horrible character at the beginning, she's always sad and lonely, but it gets better later on. I loved the small theatre-house, it was perfect for the Moomins for a few summer days. And Little My is a complete menace, I just love her. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6252040566457153460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WtJ+ApQUatvnYUaf0AOatXj0avXNgU/uVTOTI26EnzVzPWbP2Vt9Nryx2UeWZk2UGH2tKkFsy0HoGIPTgeIgtQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g8i9SdsD798rNj7ibrW9vmSWRP0ByLdsOU4k6hHw34yqJ6WElkz4MnDmoToo0GqfBB+DIo0lM8OEZTQa/pZgDA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1419249529p3/45230.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14252678964705249976"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br/><br/>Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br/><br/>Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText14252678964705249976" style="display:none"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br /><br />Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br /><br />Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3300083-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a> (1945), during World War II. She said later that the war had depressed her, and she had wanted to write something naive and innocent. Besides the <i>Moomin</i> novels and short stories, Tove Jansson also wrote and illustrated four original and highly popular picture books.<br /><br />Jansson's <i>Moomin</i> books have been translated into 33 languages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14252678964705249976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

In the United States the series beginning with Finn Family Moomintroll (first published in English in 1945) has accumulated generations of fans. Since Farrar, Straus and Giroux began reissuing the books in 1989, grateful readers old and new have been thrilled to have the stories available again. At last the final installment is being published – oddly, the only book that features none of the Moomin family themselves, though it does take place at their house. There familiar characters converge – Snufkin, the Hemulen, Fillyjonk, and others – seeking out the Moomins\' welcoming company, only to find them absent. All remain at the house, all have very different personalities that clash often, but something about their homey cohabitation during the icy winter changes each visitor in a gratifying way.
